# LoCoBench-Agent Task

## Task Information

**Task ID**: python_desktop_development_expert_021_architectural_understanding_expert_01
**Category**: architectural_understanding
**Difficulty**: expert
**Language**: python
**Context Length**: 1018897 tokens
**Files**: 73

## Task Title

Implement a System-Wide 'Focus Mode' Feature

## Description

FlockDesk is a modular desktop application designed for collaborative work. Its architecture is built upon several key principles: a central event bus for decoupled communication (`EventBus`), a plugin system for loading features as modules (`PluginManager`), a service layer for core functionalities (`SettingsService`, `AuthService`, etc.), and an MVVM (Model-View-ViewModel) pattern for the UI of each module. This scenario requires implementing a new global 'Focus Mode' feature. When a user enables Focus Mode, the application should reduce distractions from non-primary modules to help the user concentrate on a specific task (e.g., in the co-editor or whiteboard).

## Your Task

Your task is to implement the 'Focus Mode' feature across the FlockDesk application. This requires understanding and modifying multiple parts of the system, from core services to individual modules.

### Requirements:

1.  **Persistent State:** Introduce a new global setting, `focus_mode_enabled` (boolean), that persists across application restarts. The `SettingsService` is the designated component for managing user preferences.

2.  **Global Toggle:** Add a new menu item under the main 'View' menu in the application's menu bar to toggle Focus Mode on and off. This action should update the persistent state.

3.  **Event-Driven Communication:** When the Focus Mode state changes, a global event must be broadcasted across the application. You must use the existing `EventBus` for this purpose. Do not create direct dependencies between the menu bar and other modules.

4.  **Module-Level Reaction (Chat):** Modify the `Chat` module to react to Focus Mode changes. When Focus Mode is **enabled**, the chat module should visually indicate that notifications are snoozed and should suppress any new incoming message notifications.

5.  **Module-Level Reaction (Dashboard):** Modify the `Dashboard` module to react to Focus Mode changes. When Focus Mode is **enabled**, the main activity feed widget on the dashboard should be visually de-emphasized (e.g., greyed out or have its opacity lowered) to reduce visual noise.

Your implementation must respect the existing architectural patterns (Event-Driven, MVVM, Service Layer).

## Expected Approach

An expert developer would first analyze the codebase to confirm the architectural patterns. They would look for the `EventBus`, `SettingsService`, and the structure of the modules.

1.  **State Management:** The developer would identify `flockdesk/core/services/settings_service.py` and `configs/default_settings.json` as the correct places to manage the new setting. They would add `"focus_mode_enabled": false` to the JSON config and update the service to handle loading and saving this key.

2.  **Event Definition:** They would open `flockdesk/core/ipc/event_types.py` and define a new event, such as `FOCUS_MODE_CHANGED`, to standardize the communication contract.

3.  **Trigger Implementation:**
    *   They would find `flockdesk/core/shell/menu_bar.py` to add the new 'Toggle Focus Mode' QAction.
    *   To avoid putting logic in the UI, they would create a new `Command` in `flockdesk/core/shortcuts/commands.py`. This `ToggleFocusModeCommand` would be responsible for:
        a. Accessing the `SettingsService` to toggle the boolean value.
        b. Accessing the `EventBus` to publish the `FOCUS_MODE_CHANGED` event with the new state as a payload.
    *   The menu action in `menu_bar.py` would then be connected to trigger this new command.

4.  **Chat Module Modification:**
    *   The developer would identify `flockdesk/modules/chat/viewmodel/chat_vm.py` as the logic hub for the chat module.
    *   In the `ChatViewModel`'s constructor, they would subscribe to the `FOCUS_MODE_CHANGED` event on the `EventBus`.
    *   They would add a new observable property to the ViewModel, e.g., `self.is_snoozed`.
    *   The event handler would update `self.is_snoozed` based on the event payload.
    *   Finally, they would modify `flockdesk/modules/chat/view/chat_widget.py` to bind a UI element's visibility or style to the `is_snoozed` property of its ViewModel.

5.  **Dashboard Module Modification:**
    *   They would follow the exact same pattern as with the Chat module, but for the Dashboard components.
    *   They would modify `flockdesk/modules/dashboard/viewmodel/dashboard_vm.py` to subscribe to the event and manage a state property like `self.is_deemphasized`.
    *   They would then update `flockdesk/modules/dashboard/view/dashboard_widget.py` to change the styling of the activity feed based on this ViewModel property.

## Evaluation Criteria

- **Architectural Adherence (Event Bus):** Did the agent correctly use the `EventBus` for broadcasting the state change, or did it attempt to create direct, tightly-coupled calls between UI components and modules?
- **Architectural Adherence (Service Layer):** Was the `SettingsService` correctly identified and used as the single source of truth for the persistent 'Focus Mode' state?
- **Architectural Adherence (MVVM):** Were the changes in the modules correctly implemented within the ViewModel layer, with the View layer being a passive observer of the ViewModel's state?
- **Component Discovery:** Did the agent successfully locate and modify the correct, disparate set of files required for the task (settings config, event types, menu bar, command definitions, and multiple module ViewModels)?
- **Code Modularity:** Is the new code well-integrated without breaking existing patterns? Is the `ToggleFocusModeCommand` self-contained and reusable?
- **Completeness:** Does the final implementation satisfy all functional requirements: persistence, a working toggle, and the specified UI changes in both the Chat and Dashboard modules?

     1→```python
     2→"""
     3→FlockDesk – Social Workspace Orchestrator
     4→-----------------------------------------
     5→
     6→core.ipc.event_bus
     7→~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
     8→
     9→A lightweight, **process-safe** event-bus implementation that acts as the glue
    10→between the independent micro-front-ends that compose the FlockDesk desktop
    11→suite.  The implementation purposefully avoids external dependencies and
    12→relies solely on the standard library (``asyncio``/``multiprocessing``) so that
    13→plugins do not need to vendor additional wheels.
    14→
    15→Design goals
    16→============
    17→
    18→1. Publish / subscribe with topic-based routing and Unix‐shell wild-card
    19→   matching (``fnmatch``) so that a handler can listen to groups
    20→   (e.g. ``"presence.*"``).
    21→
    22→2. Support both synchronous **and** asynchronous handlers without forcing plugin
    23→   authors to learn ``asyncio``.
    24→
    25→3. Provide a *request / reply* pattern with correlation-IDs and automatic
    26→   timeout handling—essential for client–server style interactions.
    27→
    28→4. Remain safe across processes.  A *broker* process (spawned lazily and managed
    29→   via :pymod:`multiprocessing.managers`) forwards events between producer and
    30→   consumer processes transparently.
    31→
    32→5. Offer graceful shutdown semantics so that the application can quit quickly
    33→   even under heavy traffic.
    34→
    35→The broker architecture may feel heavyweight for local desktop IPC, but it
    36→guarantees that crashing micro-front-ends cannot bring down the other windows.
    37→"""
    38→
    39→from __future__ import annotations
    40→
    41→import asyncio
    42→import contextlib
    43→import fnmatch

     5→
     6→Central shortcut/command registry used by the entire FlockDesk desktop
     7→suite.  The registry provides a unified way for core components *and*
     8→external plugins to register keyboard-driven commands that can later be

    10→
    11→The implementation is intentionally *headless* – it does not create

    14→dispatching “command-invoked” events onto the global event-bus.
    15→
    16→The UI layer (or view-models in MVVM terminology) can materialise that
    17→information to visually represent the bindings and to install actual
    18→`QShortcut`s on top-level windows.
    19→
    20→Key features
    21→------------
    22→• Thread-safe, re-entrant registration/deregistration  
    23→• First-class plugin support – plugins simply call `register()`  
    24→• Hot-reloading – key-binding changes are applied at runtime  
    25→• Built-in persistence – delegates to the global Settings store  
    26→• Event-driven – command executions are emitted on the event-bus

Perfect! I now have a comprehensive understanding of the FlockDesk architecture. Let me create a detailed analysis document.

## FlockDesk Codebase Architecture Analysis - Focus Mode Implementation Guide

Based on my thorough exploration of the FlockDesk codebase, here's the complete architectural analysis you need to implement Focus Mode correctly:

---

### 1. **EventBus Implementation** (`/app/project/flockdesk/core/ipc/event_bus.py`)

**Architecture:**
- **Process-Safe Design**: Uses multiprocessing queues and a broker process (separate OS process)
- **Broker Pattern**: Fan-out architecture where one inbound queue receives events and broadcasts to multiple outbound queues (one per connected process)
- **Async-First**: Built on `asyncio` with support for both sync and async handlers

**Key Classes:**
- `Event`: Immutable dataclass with topic, payload, headers, event_id, timestamp, origin_pid
- `_Broker`: Separate OS process that forwards events from inbound to multiple outbound queues
- `EventBus`: Main singleton per-process with thread-safe subscription management
- `_Subscription`: Handle allowing unsubscribe with context manager support

**Public API:**
```python
# Singleton access
bus = EventBus.connect()  # Creates broker once per workstation

# Subscribe (sync or async handlers - both supported)
subscription = bus.subscribe(topic="chat.message.*", handler=my_handler)

# Publish (fire-and-forget)
bus.publish(topic="my.topic", payload={"data": ...})

# Request-Reply pattern with timeout
reply = await bus.request(topic="command.topic", payload=..., timeout=5.0)

# Cleanup
bus.close()
```

**Critical Patterns for Focus Mode:**
- Use wildcard patterns: `"focus.*"` matches `"focus.enabled"`, `"focus.mode.changed"`, etc.
- Both sync and async handlers are wrapped unif
... (truncated)

54-usertool_resultRead
     1→```python
     2→"""
     3→flockdesk.core.shortcuts.commands
     4→=================================
     5→
     6→Central shortcut/command registry used by the entire FlockDesk desktop
     7→suite.  The registry provides a unified way for core components *and*
     8→external plugins to register keyboard-driven commands that can later be
     9→re-mapped by the user via the settings UI.
    10→
    11→The implementation is intentionally *headless* – it does not create
    12→`QShortcut` objects itself.  Instead it focuses on keeping an in-memory
    13→catalogue of available commands, persisting user overrides, and
    14→dispatching “command-invoked” events onto the global event-bus.
    15→
    16→The UI layer (or view-models in MVVM terminology) can materialise that
    17→information to visually represent the bindings and to install actual
    18→`QShortcut`s on top-level windows.
    19→
    20→Key features
    21→------------
    22→• Thread-safe, re-entrant registration/deregistration

     2→"""
     3→FlockDesk – Social Workspace Orchestrator
     4→-----------------------------------------
     5→
     6→core.ipc.event_bus
     7→~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
     8→
     9→A lightweight, **process-safe** event-bus implementation that acts as the glue
    10→between the independent micro-front-ends that compose the FlockDesk desktop
    11→suite.  The implementation purposefully avoids external dependencies and
    12→relies solely on the standard library (``asyncio``/``multiprocessing``) so that
    13→plugins do not need to vendor additional wheels.
    14→
    15→Design goals
    16→============
    17→
    18→1. Publish / subscribe with topic-based routing and Unix‐shell wild-card
    19→   matching (``fnmatch``) so that a handler can listen to groups
    20→   (e.g. ``"presence.*"``).
    21→
    22→2. Support both synchronous **and** asynchronous handlers without forcing plugin
    23→   authors to learn ``asyncio``.
    24→
    25→3. Provide a *request / reply* pattern with correlation-IDs and automatic
    26→   timeout handling—essential for client–server style interactions.
    27→
    28→4. Remain safe across processes.  A *broker* process (spawned lazily and managed
    29→   via :pymod:`multiprocessing.managers`) forwards events between producer and
    30→   consumer processes transparently.
    31→
    32→5. Offer graceful shutdown semantics so that the application can quit quickly
    33→   even under heavy traffic.
    34→
    35→The broker architecture may feel heavyweight for local desktop IPC, but it
    36→guarantees that crashing micro-front-ends cannot bring down the other windows.
    37→"""
    38→
    39→from __future__ import annotations
    40→
    41→import asyncio
    42→import contextlib
    43→import fnmatch
  
... (truncated)

## Summary

I have completed the analysis and documented the Focus Mode feature implementation for the FlockDesk application. The solution is documented in `/logs/agent/solution.md` and includes:

**Key Findings:**

1. **Architectural Patterns Identified:**
   - **Event-Driven Architecture**: Central `EventBus` with topic-based pub/sub, wildcard matching, and process-safe communication
   - **MVVM Pattern**: ViewModels expose Qt Signals, Views bind via `connect()`
   - **Service Layer**: `SettingsService` for persistent state with namespace-based schemas
   - **Command Pattern**: `ShortcutCommandRegistry` for keyboard-triggered actions

    self._bus.subscribe(\"focus.toggle_requested\", self._on_toggle_requested)\n        # Subscribe to settings changes\n        self._bus.subscribe(\"settings.updated\", self._on_settings_changed)\n self._settings.set_value(\"focus_mode\", \"enabled\", new_state)\n        \n        # Publish state change\n        self._bus.publish(\n            Event(\n                topic=\"settings\",\n   if event.payload.get(\"namespace\") == \"focus_mode\":\n            # Apply focus mode: hide modules, disable notifications, etc.\n            settings = self._settings.get(\"focus_mode\")\n            if settings[\"enabled\"]:\n                self._apply_focus_mode(settings)\n            else:\n                self._disable_focus_mode()\n```\n\n---\n\n### 9. **Key Architectural Patterns Summary**\n\n| Pattern | Where Used | Why | Implementation |\n|---------|-----------|-----|-----------------|\n| **Event-Driven** | EventBus, services | Decoupling, async support | Pub/sub with wildcard routing |\n| **MVVM** | All modules (chat, dashboard) | Separation of concerns, testability | QObject + Qt signals |\n| **Singleton** | EventBus, SettingsService, Registry | Global state management | Thread-safe lazy initialization |\n| **Registry** | CommandRegistry, EventRegistry | Plugin extensibility | Dynamic registration at runtime |\n| **Protocol/Interface** | Menu, commands, theme manager | Loose coupling | Python Protocol types |\n| **Context Manager** | SettingsService (TransientOverride) | Resource cleanup, testing | `__enter__/__exit__` |\n| **Broker** | EventBus | Multi-process safety | Separate OS process fan-out |\n| **Decorator** | `@event`, `@register_settings_schema` | Ergonomic registration | Type-safe registration at module load |\n\n---\n\n### 10. **Critical Implementation Notes for Focus Mode**\n\n1. **Thread Safety**: All EventBus operations are thread-safe; use them from any thread\n2. **Process Safety**: Events are pickled, so payloads must be pickleable\n3. **Async Integration**: SettingsService runs in background thread; don't block UI\n4. **Event Ordering**: No guaranteed ordering between processes; use correlation_ids for request-reply\n5. **Persistence**: SettingsService auto-persists to `~/.flockdesk/focus_mode.json` (appdirs)\n6. **Hot-Reload**: Commands can be re-registered; events can be added at runtime via decorator\n7. **Error Handling**: All event handlers wrapped in exception-safe slots; exceptions logged but don't crash\n8. **Memory**: Subscriptions must be explicit; unsubscribe to avoid leaks (returned `_Subscription` object)\n\n---\n\n**File Paths (All Absolute):**\n- EventBus: `/app/project/flockdesk/core/ipc/event_bus.py`\n- EventTypes:   113\u2192class DashboardService:\n   114\u2192    \"\"\"\n   115\u2192    Orchestrates dashboard widgets and keeps the persisted layout in sync\n   116\u2192    with runtime events.  Life-cycle:\n   117\u2192\n   118\u2192        >>> service = DashboardService(event_bus, plugin_registry, state_path)\n   119\u2192        >>> await service.start()\n   120\u2192        >>> ...\n   121\u2192        >>> await service.stop()\n   122\u2192\n   123\u2192    The service is intentionally kept event-loop agnostic: it does *not*\n   124\u2192    create its own loop but expects the caller (e.g., the application\n   125\u2192    bootstrapper) to manage one.\n   126\u2192    \"\"\"\n   127\u2192\n   128\u2192    STATE_FILE_NAME = \"dashboard_state.json\"\n   129\u2192    EVENT_WIDGET_ADDED = \"dashboard.widget.added\"\n   130\u2192    EVENT_WIDGET_REMOVED = \"dashboard.widget.removed\"\n   131\u2192    EVENT_DASHBOARD_READY = \"dashboard.ready\"\n   132\u2192\n   133\u2192    # --------------------------------------------------------------------- #\n   134\u2192    # Construction & life-cycle\n   135\u2192    # --------------------------------------------------------------------- #\n   136\u2192    def __init__(\n   137\u2192        self,\n   138\u2192        event_bus: EventBus,\n   139\u2192        plugin_registry: PluginRegistry,\n   140\u2192        state_dir: Path,\n   141\u2192    ) -> None:\n   142\u2192        self._bus: EventBus = event_bus\n   143\u2192        self._plugins: PluginRegistry = plugin_registry\n   144\u2192        self._state_path: Path = state_dir / self.STATE_FILE_NAME\n   145\u2192\n   146\u2192        self._widgets: Dict[str, Widget] = {}\n   147\u2192        self._subscriptions: List[Callable[[], None]] = []\n   148\u2192\n   149\u2192        self._started = asyncio.Event()\n   150\u2192\n   151\u2192    # ------------------------------------------------------------------ #\n   152\u2192    # Public API\n   153\u2192    # ------------------------------------------------------------------ #\n   154\u2192    async def start(self) -> None:\n   155\u2192        if self._started.is_set():\n   156\u2192            _logger.debug(\"DashboardService.start() called twice \u2013 ignoring.\")\n   157\u2192            return\n   158\u2192\n   159\u2192        _logger.debug(\"DashboardService starting \u2026\")\n   160\u2192        self._setup_bus_subscriptions()\n   161\u2192        await self._restore_state()\n   162\u2192        self._started.set()\n   163\u2192        # Notify others that dashboard is ready\n   164\u2192        await self._bus.publish_async(self.EVENT_DASHBOARD_READY, {\"widget_count\": len(self._widgets)})\n   165\u2192        _logger.info(\"DashboardService started with %d widget(s).\", len(self._widgets))\n   166\u2192\n   167\u2192    async def stop(self) -> None:\n   168\u2192        if not self._started.is_set():\n   169\u2192            _logger.debug(\"DashboardService.stop() called but service was never started.\")\n   170\u2192            return\n   171\u2192\n   172\u2192        _logger.debug(\"DashboardService stopping \u2026\")\n   173\u2192        self._teardown_bus_subscriptions()\n   174\u2192        await self._persist_state()\n   175\u2192        self._started.clear()\n   176\u2192        _logger.info(\"DashboardService stopped cleanly.\")\n   177\u2192\n   178\u2192    # ------------------------------ #\n   179\u2192    # Widget commands (public)\n   180\u2192    # ------------------------------ #\n   181\u2192    async def add_widget(self, plugin_name: str, *, initial_state: dict | None = None) -> Widget:\n   182\u2192        \"\"\"\n   183\u2192        Adds a widget to the dashboard by loading its plugin entry-point.\n   184\u2192        \"\"\"\n   185\u2192        _logger.debug(\"Adding widget for plugin '%s'\u2026\", plugin_name)\n   186\u2192        meta = self._plugins.get_plugin_meta(plugin_name)\n   187\u2192        if meta.category != \"dashboard-widget\":\n   188\u2192            raise DashboardError(f\"Plugin '{plugin_name}' is not a dashboard widget (category: {meta.category!r}).\")\n   189\u2192\n   190\u2192        # Import plugin module dynamically\n   191\u2192        try:\n   192\u2192            module = self._import_plugin(meta)\n   193\u2192        except Exception as exc:  # pragma: no cover\n   194\u2192            _logger.exception(\"Failed to import plugin '%s'.\", plugin_name)\n   195\u2192            raise PluginLoadError(f\"Could not load plugin '{plugin_name}'.\") from exc\n   196\u2192\n   197\u2192        # Instantiate widget object. The plugin must provide a `create_widget`\n   198\u2192        # callable returning an initial widget state.\n   199\u2192        creator: Callable[[dict | None], dict] | None = getattr(module, meta.entrypoint, None)\n   200\u2192        if creator is None:\n   201\u2192            raise PluginLoadError(\n   202\u2192                f\"Plugin '{plugin_name}' does not expose required entry-point '{meta.entrypoint}'.\"\n   203\u2192            )\n   204\u2192\n   205\u2192        widget_state = creator(initial_state or {})\n   206\u2192        widget = Widget(id=str(uuid.uuid4()), plugin_name=plugin_name, state=widget_state)\n   207\u2192        self._widgets[widget.id] = widget\n   208\u2192\n   209\u2192        # Fire bus event (fire-and-forget)\n   210\u2192        self._bus.publish(self.EVENT_WIDGET_ADDED, widget.serialize())\n   211\u2192        await self._persist_state()\n   212\u2192        _logger.info(\"Widget %s added.\", widget.id)\n   213\u2192        return widget\n   214\u2192\n   215\u2192    async def remove_widget(self, widget_id: str) -> None:\n   216\u2192        \"\"\"\n   217\u2192        Removes the widget from dashboard.  Silently ignores unknown ids.\n   218\u2192        \"\"\"\n   219\u2192        widget = self._widgets.pop(widget_id, None)\n   220\u2192        if widget is None:\n   221\u2192            _logger.warning(\"Widget '%s' not found \u2013 nothing to remove.\", widget_id)\n   222\u2192            return\n   223\u2192\n   224\u2192        self._bus.publish(self.EVENT_WIDGET_REMOVED, {\"id\": widget_id})\n   225\u2192        await self._persist_state()\n   226\u2192        _logger.info(\"Widget %s removed.\", widget_id)\n   227\u2192\n   228\u2192    def list_widgets(self) -> List[Widget]:\n   229\u2192        \"\"\"Return a copy of currently active widgets (read-only).\"\"\"\n   230\u2192        return list(self._widgets.values())\n   231\u2192\n   232\u2192    # ------------------------------------------------------------------ #\n   233\u2192    # Internal helpers\n   234\u2192    # ------------------------------------------------------------------ #\n   235\u2192    def _import_plugin(self, meta: PluginMeta) -> ModuleType:\n   236\u2192        \"\"\"\n   237\u2192        Import or reload the plugin module, depending on whether it's already\n   238\u2192        present in `sys.modules`.  This enables hot-reloading without restarting\n   239\u2192        the whole application.\n   240\u2192        \"\"\"\n   241\u2192        if meta.module in sys.modules:\n   242\u2192            _logger.debug(\"Reloading plugin module %s \u2026\", meta.module)\n   243\u2192            return importlib.reload(sys.modules[meta.module])\n   244\u2192        _logger.debug(\"Importing plugin module %s \u2026\", meta.module)\n   245\u2192        return importlib.import_module(meta.module)\n   246\u2192\n   247\u2192    # ------------------------------ #\n   248\u2192    # State persistence\n   249\u2192    # ------------------------------ #\n   250\u2192    async def _persist_state(self) -> None:\n   251\u2192        \"\"\"\n   252\u2192        Persist current widget layout to a JSON file.  The operation is off-loaded\n   253\u2192        to a thread-pool to avoid blocking the event-loop on slower file-systems.\n   254\u2192        \"\"\"\n   255\u2192        widgets_data = [w.serialize() for w in self._widgets.values()]\n   256\u2192        loop = asyncio.get_running_loop()\n   257\u2192        await loop.run_in_executor(None, self._write_state_file, widgets_data)\n   258\u2192\n   259\u2192    async def _restore_state(self) -> None:\n   260\u2192        \"\"\"\n   261\u2192        Load dashboard widgets from state-file.  Widgets whose plugins cannot be\n   262\u2192        loaded are skipped with a warning.\n   263\u2192        \"\"\"\n   264\u2192        loop = asyncio.get_running_loop()\n   265\u2192        widgets_data: List[dict] | None = await loop.run_in_executor(None, self._read_state_file)\n   266\u2192\n   267\u2192        if not widgets_data:\n   268\u2192            _logger.debug(\"No persisted dashboard state found.\")\n   269\u2192            return\n   270\u2192\n   271\u2192        for raw in widgets_data:\n   272\u2192            with suppress(Exception):\n   273\u2192                widget = Widget.deserialize(raw)\n   274\u2192                # Best-effort restore; skip if plugin fails to load.\n   275\u2192                with suppress(Exception):\n   276\u2192                    await self.add_widget(widget.plugin_name, initial_state=widget.state)\n   277\u2192                    # Overwrite generated id with persisted one so references remain stable\n   278\u2192                    self._widgets[widget.id].id = widget.id\n   279\u2192\n   280\u2192        _logger.debug(\"Restored %d widget(s) from persisted state.\", len(self._widgets))\n   281\u2192\n   282\u2192    def _write_state_file(self, data: List[dict]) -> None:\n   283\u2192        try:\n   284\u2192            self._state_path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)\n   285\u2192            self._state_path.write_text(json.dumps(data, indent=2), encoding=\"utf-8\")\n   286\u2192            _logger.debug(\"Dashboard state written to %s.\", self._state_path)\n   287\u2192        except Exception:  # pragma: no cover\n   288\u2192            _logger.exception(\"Failed to write dashboard state to disk.\")\n   289\u2192\n   290\u2192    def _read_state_file(self) -> List[dict] | None:\n   291\u2192        if not self._state_path.exists():\n   292\u2192            return None\n   293\u2192        try:\n   294\u2192            return json.loads(self._state_path.read_text(encoding=\"utf-8\"))\n   295\u2192        except Exception:  # pragma: no cover\n   296\u2192            _logger.exception(\"Failed to read dashboard state \u2013 file will be ignored.\")\n   297\u2192            return None\n   298\u2192\n   299\u2192    # ------------------------------ #\n   300\u2192    # Event-bus subscriptions\n   301\u2192    # ------------------------------ #\n   302\u2192    def _setup_bus_subscriptions(self) -> None:\n   303\u2192        \"\"\"\n   304\u2192        Connects to the internal event-bus so that the service reacts to\n   305\u2192        cross-cutting events (e.g., plugin reloads).\n   306\u2192        \"\"\"\n   307\u2192        self._subscriptions.append(\n   308\u2192            self._bus.subscribe(\"plugins.reloaded\", self._on_plugin_reloaded)\n   309\u2192        )\n   310\u2192        self._subscriptions.append(\n   311\u2192            self._bus.subscribe(\"settings.theme.changed\", self._on_theme_changed)\n   312\u2192        )\n   313\u2192        _logger.debug(\"DashboardService subscribed to %d bus topic(s).\", len(self._subscriptions))\n   314\u2192\n   315\u2192    def _teardown_bus_subscriptions(self) -> None:\n   316\u2192        for unsubscribe in self._subscriptions:\n   317\u2192            with suppress(Exception):\n   318\u2192                unsubscribe()\n   319\u2192        self._subscriptions.clear()\n   320\u2192        _logger.debug(\"DashboardService unsubscribed from all bus topics.\")\n   321\u2192\n   322\u2192    # ------------------------------ #\n   323\u2192    # Event-handlers\n   324\u2192    # ------------------------------ #\n   325\u2192    def _on_plugin_reloaded(self, topic: str, payload: Any) -> None:\n   326\u2192        \"\"\"\n   327\u2192        If a plugin is hot-reloaded, rebuild the corresponding widgets so that\n   328\u2192        users immediately see the new version.\n   329\u2192        \"\"\"\n   330\u2192        plugin_name: str = payload.get(\"name\") if isinstance(payload, dict) else str(payload)\n   331\u2192        affected = [w for w in self._widgets.values() if w.plugin_name == plugin_name]\n   332\u2192        if not affected:\n   333\u2192            return\n   334\u2192\n   335\u2192        _logger.info(\"Plugin '%s' reloaded \u2013 refreshing %d dashboard widget(s)\u2026\", plugin_name, len(affected))\n   336\u2192        # Remove & re-add widgets, preserving order/state.\n   337\u2192        asyncio.create_task(self._refresh_widgets(affected))\n   338\u2192\n   339\u2192    def _on_theme_changed(self, topic: str, payload: Any) -> None:\n   340\u2192        \"\"\"\n   341\u2192        Relay theme change to all widgets (which may adjust colours, icons, \u2026);\n   342\u2192        the actual rendering happens in each widget's view-model.\n   343\u2192        \"\"\"\n   344\u2192        theme_name: str = payload.get(\"theme\")\n   345\u2192        for widget in self._widgets.values():\n   346\u2192            self._bus.publish(f\"widget.{widget.id}.theme_changed\", {\"theme\": theme_name})\n   347\u2192\n   348\u2192    # ------------------------------ #\n   349\u2192    # Complex background tasks\n   350\u2192    # ------------------------------ #\n   351\u2192    async def _refresh_widgets(self, widgets: List[Widget]) -> None:\n   352\u2192        \"\"\"\n   353\u2192        Remove & re-add widgets.  This is done sequentially so that the order in\n   354\u2192        the dashboard remains stable.\n   355\u2192        \"\"\"\n   356\u2192        for widget in widgets:\n   357\u2192            await self.remove_widget(widget.id)\n   358\u2192            # SettingsService, namespace: str) -> None:\n        self._service = service\n        self._namespace = namespace\n        self._original_instance: Optional[Any] = None\n\n    def __enter__(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:\n        with self._service._lock:\n            inst = self._service._instances.get(self._namespace)\n            if inst is None:\n                raise SettingsServiceError(\n                    f\"Cannot edit unknown namespace '{self._namespace}'.\"\n                )\n            # Deep-copy to preserve original\n            self._original_instance = dataclasses.replace(inst)\n            return dataclasses.asdict(inst)\n\n    def __exit__(self, exc_type, exc_val, exc_tb) -> None:\n        with self._service._lock:\n            if self._original_instance is not None:\n                self._service._instances[self._namespace] = self._original_instance\n                self._service._dirty_namespaces.discard(self._namespace)\n                _logger.debug(\n                    \"Transient overrides for namespace '%s' reverted.\",\n                    self._namespace,\n                )\n```",

The registry provides a unified way for core components *and*\nexternal plugins to register keyboard-driven commands that can later be\nre-mapped by the user via the settings UI.\n\nThe implementation is intentionally *headless* \u2013 it does not create\n`QShortcut` objects itself.  Instead it focuses on keeping an in-memory\ncatalogue of available commands, persisting user overrides, and\ndispatching \u201ccommand-invoked\u201d events onto the global event-bus.\n\nThe UI layer (or view-models in MVVM terminology) can materialise that\ninformation to visually represent the bindings and to install actual\n`QShortcut`s on top-level windows.\n\nKey features\n------------\n\u2022 Thread-safe, re-entrant registration/deregistration  \n\u2022 First-class plugin support \u2013 plugins simply call `register()`  \n\u2022 Hot-reloading \u2013 key-binding changes are applied at runtime  \n\u2022 Built-in persistence \u2013 delegates to the global Settings store  \n\u2022 Event-driven \u2013 command executions are emitted on the event-bus\n\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport logging\nimport threading\nfrom dataclasses import dataclass, field\nfrom typing import Callable, Dict, Iterable, List, Optional\n\nfrom PySide6.QtGui import QKeySequence\nfrom PySide6.QtWidgets import QShortcut, QWidget\nfrom PySide6.QtCore import Qt, QObject, Signal\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Global logger for this module\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\nlogger = logging.getLogger(__name__)\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Event-bus integration\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\ntry:\n    # ``QKeySequence(sequence)`` (e.g. ``\"Ctrl+Shift+P\"``).\n        \"\"\"\n        if isinstance(sequence, str):\n            sequence = QKeySequence(sequence)\n\n        with self._lock:\n The implementation purposefully avoids external dependencies and\nrelies solely on the standard library (``asyncio``/``multiprocessing``) so that\nplugins do not need to vendor additional wheels.\n\nDesign goals\n============\n\n1. Publish / subscribe with topic-based routing and Unix\u2010shell wild-card\n   matching (``fnmatch``) so that a handler can listen to groups\n   (e.g. ``\"presence.*\"``).\n\n2. Support both synchronous **and** asynchronous handlers without forcing plugin\n   authors to learn ``asyncio``.\n\n3. Provide a *request / reply* pattern with correlation-IDs and automatic\n   timeout handling\u2014essential for client\u2013server style interactions.\n\n4. Remain safe across processes.  A *broker* process (spawned lazily and managed\n   via :pymod:`multiprocessing.managers`) forwards events between producer and\n   consumer processes transparently.\n\n5. Offer graceful shutdown semantics so that the application can quit quickly\n   even under heavy traffic.\n\nThe broker architecture may feel heavyweight for local desktop IPC, but it\nguarantees that Keep sync handler as is, wrap non-coroutine functions so that we can\n        # `await` them uniformly.\n        if not inspect.iscoroutinefunction(handler):\n\n            async def _async_adapter(evt: Event, _h=handler) -> None:\n                await self._loop.run_in_executor(None, _h, evt)\n\n            adapted: Handler = _async_adapter\n        else:\n            adapted = handler  # Internal helpers\n    # ------------------------------------------------------------------#\n    def _remove_handler(self, topic: str, handler: Handler) -> None:\n        async def _remove() -> None:\n            async with self._h_lock:\n                lst = self._handlers.get(topic, [])\n                if handler in lst:\n                    lst.remove(handler)\n\n        asyncio.run_coroutine_threadsafe(_remove(), self._loop).result()\n\n    def _ensure_dispatcher(self) -> None:\n        if self._dispatch_task is None or self._dispatch_task.done():\n            self._dispatch_task = self._loop.create_task(self._dispatcher())\n\n    async def _dispatcher(self) -> None:\n        \"\"\"\n        Background coroutine that consumes events from the *outbound* queue and\n        delivers them to pattern-matched handlers.\n        \"\"\"\n        _log.debug(\"EventBus dispatcher started (thread=%s)\", threading.current_thread().name)\n        while not self._shutdown_evt.is_set():\n            try:\n                # Flatten into (topic_pattern, handlers[])\n            items: List[Tuple[str, List[Handler]]] = list(self._handlers.items())\n\n        coros: List[Awaitable[None]] = []\n\n        for pattern, handlers in items:\n            if fnmatch.fnmatchcase(evt.topic, pattern):\n                coros.extend(h(evt) for h in handlers)\n\n        if not coros:\n            return  # pragma: no cover\n    logging.basicConfig(level=logging.DEBUG)\n\n    async def main() -> None:\n        bus = get_event_bus()\n\n        # Example async handler\n        async def on_presence(evt: Event) -> None:\n            print(\"[async] received\", evt.topic, evt.payload)\n\n        # Example sync handler\n        def on_any(evt: Event) -> None:\n            print(\"[sync ] saw\", evt.topic, evt.payload)\n\n        bus.subscribe(\"presence.*\", on_presence)\n        bus.subscribe(\"**\", on_any)\n\n        # Publish from different thread\n        def _publisher() -> None:\n            b = get_event_bus()\n            b.publish(\"presence.updated\", {\"user\": \"alice\", \"status\": \"online\"})\n\n        threading.Thread(target=_publisher, daemon=True).start()\n\n        await asyncio.sleep(1.0)\n        bus.close()\n\n    asyncio.run(main())\n```",

-------- Qt Signals ----------------------------------------------------#\n    messageAdded = QtCore.Signal(ChatMessage)  # new message appended\n    messageReplaced = QtCore.Signal(ChatMessage)  # edited or updated\n    typingStatusChanged = QtCore.Signal(str, bool)  # user_id, is_typing\n    errorOccurred = QtCore.Signal(str)  # human-readable error string\n    historyLoaded = QtCore.Signal(list)  # list[ChatMessage]\n\n    # -----------------------------------------------------------------------#\n    def __init__(self, channel_id: str, event_bus: EventBus, parent=None) -> None:\n        super().__init__(parent)\n        self._channel_id: str = channel_id\n        self._event_bus: EventBus = event_bus\n        self._messages: list[ChatMessage] = []\n\n        # drafts/<user>/<channel>.json\n        self._draft_path: Path = (\n            Path(settings.get(\"user_data_dir\", \"~/.flockdesk\")).expanduser()\n            / \"drafts\"\n            / f\"{settings.get('user_id', 'anonymous')}\"\n            / f\"{channel_id}.json\"\n        )\n\n        self._typing_users: Dict[str, QtCore.QTimer] = {}\n        self._lock = threading.RLock()\n\n        self._register_event_subscriptions()\n        self._restore_draft_async()\n\n    # -----------------------------------------------------------------------#\n    # API surface for Controllers\n    # -----------------------------------------------------------------------#\n    def history(self) -> list[ChatMessage]:\n        \"\"\"Return a copy of the current message history.\"\"\"\n        with self._lock:\n            return list(self._messages)\n\n    def send_message(self, content: str, attachments: Optional[List[Path]] = None) -> None:\n        \"\"\"\n        Send a message to the current channel.\n\n        The actual network interaction is delegated to the domain layer\n        via the event-bus. We optimistically append the message locally\n        and mark it as `is_outgoing=True`; once the server acknowledges\n        (or rejects) the message we will replace/update it.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not content and not attachments:\n            _log.debug(\"Empty message suppressed\")\n            return\n\n        msg_id = f\"tmp-{datetime.now(tz=timezone.utc).timestamp()}\"\n        attachments = attachments or []\n        outgoing = ChatMessage(\n            msg_id=msg_id,\n            channel_id=self._channel_id,\n            sender_id=settings.get(\"user_id\", \"anonymous\"),\n            sender_display=settings.get(\"user_display\", \"Me\"),\n            content=content,\n            timestamp=datetime.now(tz=timezone.utc),\n            is_outgoing=True,\n            attachments=attachments,\n        )\n\n        self._append_message(outgoing)\n\n        # Publish to domain event-bus (fire-and-forget)\n        _log.debug(\"Publishing OutgoingMessage event: %s\", outgoing.msg_id)\n        self._event_bus.publish(\n            Event(\n                topic=\"chat.outgoing\",\n                payload=outgoing.serialize(),\n                replayable=False,\n            )\n        )\n\n        # Clear persisted draft for this channel\n        self._clear_draft_file()\n\n    def start_typing(self) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Publish typing indicator event when user starts typing.\"\"\"\n        self._event_bus.publish(\n            Event(\n                topic=\"chat.typing\",\n                payload={\"channel_id\": self._channel_id, \"user_id\": settings.get(\"user_id\")},\n            )\n        )\n\n    def persist_draft(self, draft_text: str) -> None:\n        \"\"\"\n        Persist unsent draft on disk.\n\n        Called from the Controller on text-changed events.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not draft_text.strip():\n            self._clear_draft_file()\n            return\n\n        self._draft_path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)\n        try:\n            self._draft_path.write_text(\n                json.dumps({\"draft\": draft_text, \"timestamp\": datetime.now().isoformat()}),\n                encoding=\"utf-8\",\n            )\n            _log.debug(\"Draft persisted to %s\", self._draft_path)\n        except OSError as exc:\n            _log.warning(\"Failed to write draft file: %s\", exc)\n\n    # -----------------------------------------------------------------------#\n    # Internal helpers\n    # -----------------------------------------------------------------------#\n    def _register_event_subscriptions(self) -> None:\n        \"\"\"\n        Subscribe to the global EventBus for chat-related events.\n\n        We keep the subscription tokens so we can unsubscribe\n        when the View-Model is deleted / the window is closed.\n        \"\"\"\n\n        # Incoming messages\n        self._event_bus.subscribe(\n            \"chat.incoming\",\n            self._on_incoming_message,\n            group=f\"vm_{self._channel_id}\",\n        )\n\n        # Delivery acknowledgements for optimistic updates\n        self._event_bus.subscribe(\n            \"chat.outgoing.confirmation\",\n            self._on_delivery_confirmation,\n            group=f\"vm_{self._channel_id}\",\n        )\n\n        # Typing indicators\n        self._event_bus.subscribe(\n            \"chat.typing\",\n            self._on_typing_indicator,\n            group=f\"vm_{self._channel_id}\",\n        )\n\n        # Synchronised edits / deletions\n        self._event_bus.subscribe(\n            \"chat.message.updated\",\n            self._on_remote_update,\n            group=f\"vm_{self._channel_id}\",\n        )\n\n    # -----------------------------------------------------------------------#\n    def _append_message(self, message: ChatMessage) -> None:\n        with self._lock:\n            self._messages.append(message)\n        self.messageAdded.emit(message)\n\n    # -----------------------------------------------------------------------#\n    # Event-bus callback handlers\n    # -----------------------------------------------------------------------#\n    def _on_incoming_message(self, event: Event) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Handle new message events from other users.\"\"\"\n        payload = event.payload\n        if payload[\"channel_id\"] != self._channel_id:\n            return\n\n        msg = ChatMessage(\n            msg_id=payload[\"msg_id\"],\n            channel_id=payload[\"channel_id\"],\n            sender_id=payload[\"sender_id\"],\n            sender_display=payload[\"sender_display\"],\n            content=payload[\"content\"],\n            timestamp=datetime.fromisoformat(payload[\"timestamp\"]),\n            attachments=[Path(p) for p in payload.get(\"attachments\", [])],\n        )\n        self._append_message(msg)\n\n    # -----------------------------------------------------------------------#\n    def _on_delivery_confirmation(self, event: Event) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Replace optimistic message with definitive server copy.\"\"\"\n        payload = event.payload\n        if payload[\"channel_id\"] != self._channel_id:\n            return\n\n        tmp_id = payload[\"tmp_id\"]\n        real_id = payload[\"msg_id\"]\n\n        with self._lock:\n            for idx, m in enumerate(self._messages):\n                if m.msg_id == tmp_id:\n                    updated = ChatMessage(\n                        msg_id=real_id,\n                        channel_id=m.channel_id,\n                        sender_id=m.sender_id,\n                        sender_display=m.sender_display,\n                        content=m.content,\n                        timestamp=datetime.fromisoformat(payload[\"timestamp\"]),\n                        is_outgoing=False,\n                        attachments=m.attachments,\n                    )\n                    self._messages[idx] = updated\n                    _log.debug(\"Optimistic message %s replaced by %s\", tmp_id, real_id)\n                    self.messageReplaced.emit(updated)\n                    break\n\n    # -----------------------------------------------------------------------#\n    def _on_typing_indicator(self, event: Event) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Update typing indicator map & emit signal.\"\"\"\n        payload = event.payload\n        if payload[\"channel_id\"] != self._channel_id:\n            return\n\n        user_id = payload[\"user_id\"]\n        if user_id == settings.get(\"user_id\"):\n            return  # ignore self typing\n\n        # Reset/Start debounce timer for this user\n        timer = self._typing_users.get(user_id)\n        if timer is None:\n            timer = QtCore.QTimer(self)\n            timer.setSingleShot(True)\n            timer.timeout.connect(lambda uid=user_id: self._emit_typing_end(uid))\n            self._typing_users[user_id] = timer\n            self.typingStatusChanged.emit(user_id, True)\n\n        timer.start(3000)  # 3s window\n\n    def _emit_typing_end(self, user_id: str) -> None:\n        self.typingStatusChanged.emit(user_id, False)\n        self._typing_users.pop(user_id, None)\n\n    # -----------------------------------------------------------------------#\n    def _on_remote_update(self, event: Event) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Handle remote edits or deletions.\"\"\"\n        payload = event.payload\n        if payload[\"channel_id\"] != self._channel_id:\n            return\n\n        with self._lock:\n            for idx, m in enumerate(self._messages):\n                if m.msg_id == payload[\"msg_id\"]:\n                    updated = ChatMessage(\n                        msg_id=m.msg_id,\n                        channel_id=m.channel_id,\n                        sender_id=m.sender_id,\n                        sender_display=m.sender_display,\n                        content=payload.get(\"content\", m.content),\n                        timestamp=m.timestamp,\n                        edited=True,\n                        attachments=[Path(p) for p in payload.get(\"attachments\", [])],\n                    )\n                    self._messages[idx] = updated\n                    self.messageReplaced.emit(updated)\n                    _log.debug(\"Message %s updated from remote\", m.msg_id)\n                    break\n\n    # -----------------------------------------------------------------------#\n    # Draft persistence\n    # -----------------------------------------------------------------------#\n    def _restore_draft_async(self) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Restore draft in a background thread to keep UI responsive.\"\"\"\n\n        def _worker(vm: \"ChatViewModel\") -> None:\n            if vm._draft_path.exists():\n                try:\n                    data = json.loads(vm._draft_path.read_text(encoding=\"utf-8\"))\n                    draft = data.get(\"draft\", \"\")\n                    _log.debug(\"Draft restored for channel %s\", vm._channel_id)\n                    # Emit via Qt to avoid cross-thread issues\n                    QtCore.QMetaObject.invokeMethod(\n                        vm,\n                        \"_emit_draft_restored\",\n                        QtCore.Qt.QueuedConnection,\n                        QtCore.Q_ARG(str, draft),\n                    )\n                except (OSError, json.JSONDecodeError) as exc:\n                    _log.warning(\"Failed to restore draft: %s\", exc)\n\n        threading.Thread(target=_worker, args=(self,), daemon=True).start()\n\n    @QtCore.Slot(str)\n    def _emit_draft_restored(self, text: str) -> None:\n        self.historyLoaded.emit([])  # just to notify view to attach draft text\n\n    def _clear_draft_file(self) -> None:\n        try:\n            if self._draft_path.exists():\n                self._draft_path.unlink(missing_ok=True)\n                _log.debug(\"Draft cleared for channel %s\", self._channel_id)\n        except OSError as exc:\n            _log.warning(\"Failed to clear draft file: %s\", exc)\n\n    # -----------------------------------------------------------------------#\n    # Qt Object Life-Cycle\n    # -----------------------------------------------------------------------#\n    def __del__(self) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Ensure we cleanly unsubscribe from the EventBus.\"\"\"\n        try:\n            self._event_bus.unsubscribe_group(f\"vm_{self._channel_id}\")\n        except Exception:  # pragma: no cover\n            pass  # During interpreter shutdown objects may be gone\n\n\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------#\n# Factory (Dependency Injection ready)\n# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------#\ndef create_chat_viewmodel(channel_id: str, event_bus: EventBus) -> ChatViewModel:\n    \"\"\"\n    Factory helper so the app\u2019s DI container can easily inject dependencies.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    ChatViewModel\n        Ready-to-use instance with subscriptions in place.\n    \"\"\"\n    vm = ChatViewModel(channel_id=channel_id, event_bus=event_bus)\n    return vm\n```",

Raises KeyError if command\n        is unknown; any exception from the command itself is propagated.\n        \"\"\"\n        if name not in self._commands:\n            raise KeyError(f\"Unknown command: {name}\")\n\n        _logger.debug(\"Executing command '%s' with args=%s kwargs=%s\",\n                      name, args, kwargs)\n        return self._commands[name](*args, **kwargs)\n\n    # Emits widgetsChanged/themeChanged\n        on success.\n        \"\"\"\n        file_path = self._layout_file()\n        if not file_path.exists():\n            _logger.info(\"No persisted layout found (%s), skipping restore\",\n                         file_path)\n            return\n\n        _logger.info(\"Restoring dashboard layout from '%s'\", file_path)\n        try:\n            raw = file_path.read_text(encoding=\"utf-8\")\n            self._state = DashboardState.from_json(raw)\n            self.widgetsChanged.emit(self.widgets)\n            self.themeChanged.emit(self._state.active_theme)\n        except Exception as exc:  # pragma: no cover\n            _logger.exception(\"Failed restoring layout: %s\", exc)\n            self.errorOccurred.emit(f\"Restore failed: {exc}\")\n\n    def save_layout_sync(self) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Blocking save helper, safe to call from worker threads.\"\"\"\n        file_path = self._layout_file()\n        _logger.debug(\"Persisting dashboard layout to '%s'\", file_path)\n        try:\n            file_path.write_text(self._state.to_json(), encoding=\"utf-8\")\n        except Exception as exc:  # pragma: no cover\n            _logger.exception(\"Saving layout failed: %s\", exc)\n            # Forward to UI; we don't re-raise to avoid crashing the caller\n            self.errorOccurred.emit(f\"Saving layout failed: {exc}\")\n\n    def save_layout_async(self) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Schedule an asynchronous layout persistence in a thread-pool.\"\"\"\n        async def _task() -> None:\n            self._set_busy(True)\n            try:\n                await self._loop.run_in_executor(None, self.save_layout_sync)\n            finally:\n                self._set_busy(False)\n\n        asyncio.ensure_future(_task(), loop=self._loop)\n\n    def _trigger_auto_save(self) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Reset debounce timer to delay disk writes during rapid changes.\"\"\"\n        self._auto_save_timer.start()\n\n    # -------------------------- Event-Bus glue ------------------------------#\n    def _register_event_listeners(self) -> None:\n        self._subscriptions.extend([\n            self._event_bus.subscribe(\"plugin.loaded\", self._on_plugin_loaded),\n            self._event_bus.subscribe(\"plugin.unloaded\", self._on_plugin_unloaded),\n            self._event_bus.subscribe(\"theme.external_switch\",\n                                      self._on_external_theme_switch),\n        ])\n\n    async def _on_plugin_loaded(self, *, plugin_id: str, **_: Any) -> None:\n        # Example reaction: automatically add analytics widget when plugin loads\n        _logger.debug(\"Handling plugin.loaded for '%s'\", plugin_id)\n        meta = self._plugin_manager.metadata_for(plugin_id)\n        if meta.auto_attach_to_dashboard:\n            self.add_widget(plugin_id)\n\n    async def _on_plugin_unloaded(self, *, plugin_id: str, **_: Any) -> None:\n        _logger.debug(\"Handling plugin.unloaded for '%s'\", plugin_id)\n        stale = [w.id for w in self._state.widgets if w.plugin_id == plugin_id]\n        for wid in stale:\n            self.remove_widget(wid)\n\n    async def _on_external_theme_switch(self, *, theme: str, **_: Any) -> None:\n        # Keep internal state in sync with theme changes initiated elsewhere\n        _logger.debug(\"Received external theme switch '%s'\", theme)\n        self.switch_theme(theme)\n\n    # --------------------------- Misc helpers -------------------------------#\n    def _set_busy(self, value: bool) -> None:\n        if self._busy != value:\n            self._busy = value\n            self.busyChanged.emit(value)\n\n    def dispose(self) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Explicitly unsubscribe from the event-bus (call on window close).\"\"\"\n        for sub in self._subscriptions:\n            try:\n                sub.unsubscribe()\n            except Exception:  # pragma: no cover\n                _logger.debug(\"Subscription cleanup failed\", exc_info=True)\n        self._subscriptions.clear()\n\n    # -------------------------- Dunder helpers ------------------------------#\n    def __del__(self) -> None:  # pragma: no cover\n        # Best-effort dispose; avoid reference cycles\n        try:\n            self.dispose()\n        except Exception:\n            pass\n```",

Each card is a plugin that exposes a QWidget\nand registers itself to the internal event-bus.  Users can re-arrange,\nremove, and add cards simply by dragging & dropping new plugins from the\nplugin-palette or by right-clicking a card and selecting *Remove*.\n\nDesign goals\n------------\n1. MVVM separation \u2013 the widget delegates all non-UI work to the\n   DashboardViewModel.\n2. Event driven \u2013 real-time updates via the global EventBus.\n3. Plugin friendly \u2013 cards are loaded/unloaded via the PluginManager.\n4. Robustness \u2013 every plugin is sandboxed; a faulty widget is replaced\n   with a red *crash card* rather than crashing the entire dashboard.\n\nThe implementation purposefully stays clear of concrete business-logic.\nProjects embedding this component must provide:\n\n* flockdesk.core.event_bus.EventBus              (pub/sub)\n* flockdesk.core.plugins.manager.PluginManager   (plugin life-cycle)\n* flockdesk.core.settings.AppSettings            (persistent settings)\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport asyncio\nimport logging\nimport traceback\nfrom contextlib DashboardViewModel(QObject):\n    \"\"\"\n    The *VM* coordinating event-bus messages, plugin life-cycle and layout\n    persistence.  The view (DashboardWidget) only performs tasks strictly\n    related to UI rendering.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    # Signals exposed to the view\n    themeChanged = Signal(str)  # dark / light / custom-name\n    settingsChanged = Signal()\n    cardCrashed = Signal(str)  # plugin_id -> CardMeta\n        self._cards: Dict[str, CardMeta] = {}\n\n        self._subscribe_events()\n\n    # --------------------------------------------------------------------- API\n\n    def load_initial_cards(self) -> None:\n        \"\"\"\n        Load cards remembered from the previous session, honoring the user\u2019s\n        persistent layout.\n        \"\"\"\n        stored_cards = self._settings.dashboard.cards\n        logger.debug(\"Loading persisted dashboard cards: %s\", stored_cards)\n        for plugin_id in stored_cards:\n            self.add_card(plugin_id)\n\n    def add_card(self, plugin_id: str) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Instantiate a plugin widget and register it as a CardMeta.\"\"\"\n        if plugin_id in self._cards:\n            logger.info(\"Card for plugin '%s' already present \u2013 skipping\", plugin_id)\n            return\n        try:\n            plugin_cls: Type[\"BasePlugin\"] = self._plugin_manager.get_plugin(plugin_id)\n            plugin: \"BasePlugin\" = plugin_cls()\n            widget = plugin.build_widget()  # type: ignore[attr-defined]\n        except Exception as exc:  # noqa: BLE001\n            logger.error(\"Could not instantiate plugin '%s': %s\", plugin_id, exc)\n            self.cardCrashed.emit(plugin_id)\n            return\n\n        meta = CardMeta(\n            plugin_id=plugin_id,\n            plugin_name=plugin.meta.name,  # type: ignore[attr-defined]\n            widget=widget,\n        )\n        self._cards[plugin_id] = meta\n        self._settings.dashboard.cards.append(plugin_id)\n        self._settings.save()\n\n        # Must be emitted so the view can insert the widget in the layout.\n        self.settingsChanged.emit()\n\n    def remove_card(self, plugin_id: str) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Remove plugin card from internal model and persist change.\"\"\"\n        if plugin_id not in self._cards:\n            return\n\n        meta = self._cards.pop(plugin_id)\n        meta.widget.deleteLater()\n\n        with suppress(ValueError):\n            self._settings.dashboard.cards.remove(plugin_id)\n        self._settings.save()\n        self.settingsChanged.emit()\n\n    def cards(self) -> Dict[str, CardMeta]:\n        \"\"\"Return the currently active cards.\"\"\"\n        return self._cards\n\n    # ----------------------------------------------------------------- Events\n\n    def _subscribe_events(self) -> None:\n        # Theme changes\n        self._event_bus.subscribe(\"ui.theme.changed\", self._on_theme_changed)\n        # Global settings updated\n        self._event_bus.subscribe(\"settings.updated\", self._on_settings_updated)\n\n    async def _on_theme_changed(self, event: \"Event\") -> None:  # noqa: D401\n        theme_name = event.payload.get(\"theme\")\n        logger.debug(\"Theme change event received: %s\", theme_name)\n        self.themeChanged.emit(theme_name)\n\n    async def _on_settings_updated(self, event: \"Event\") -> None:  # TODO: make configurable\n\n    def __init__(self, view_model: Optional[DashboardViewModel] = None) -> None:\n        super().__init__()\n\n        # If not injected (unit-tests), create a default one\n        self._vm = view_model or DashboardViewModel()\n\n        self.setAcceptDrops(True)\n        self.setObjectName(\"flockdeskDashboard\")\n        self._build_ui()\n\n        # ------------------------------------------------------------ Card helpers\n\n    def _handle_card_crash(self, plugin_id: str) -> None:\n        logger.debug(\"Handling crash of plugin '%s'\", plugin_id)\n        crash_card = CrashCard(plugin_id)\n        self._insert_widget(crash_card)\n\n    def _rebuild_cards(self) -> None:\n        \"\"\"\n        Re-create the grid whenever cards were added/removed or when a plugin\n        crashed.\n        \"\"\"\n        while self._grid.count():\n            item = self._grid.takeAt(0)\n            if widget := item.widget():\n                widget.setParent(None)\n                widget.deleteLater()\n\n        col, row = 0, 0\n        for meta in self._vm.cards().values():\n            self._insert_widget(meta.widget, row=row, col=col)\n            col += 1\n            if col >= self.GRID_COLUMNS:\n                col = 0\n                row += 1\n\n        self._grid.setRowStretch(row + 1, 1)\n        self._grid.setColumnStretch(self.GRID_COLUMNS, 1)\n        self.updateGeometry()\n\n    def _insert_widget(self, widget: QWidget, *, row: int | None = None, col: int | None = None) -> None:\n        \"\"\"\n        Insert `widget` into the next free cell unless `row/col` is provided.\n        \"\"\"\n        if row is None or col is None:\n            position = self._next_free_cell()\n            row, col = position\n\n        widget.setSizePolicy(QSizePolicy.Expanding, QSizePolicy.Expanding)\n        self._grid.addWidget(widget, row, col)\n        logger.debug(\"Inserted widget at row=%s col=%s\", row, col)\n\n    def _next_free_cell(self) -> tuple[int, int]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Calculate the next free slot in the grid using a simple left-to-right,\n        top-to-bottom algorithm.\n        \"\"\"\n        count = self._grid.count()\n        col = count % self.GRID_COLUMNS\n        row = count // self.GRID_COLUMNS\n        return row, col\n\n    # ----------------------------------------------------------- Drag & drop\n\n    def dragEnterEvent(self, event: QDragEnterEvent) -> None:\n        mime: QMimeData = event.mimeData()\n        if mime.hasFormat(DashboardViewModel.MIME_TYPE):\n            event.setDropAction(Qt.CopyAction)\n            event.acceptProposedAction()\n        else:\n            super().dragEnterEvent(event)\n\n    def dropEvent(self, event: QDropEvent) -> None:\n        mime: QMimeData = event.mimeData()\n        if not mime.hasFormat(DashboardViewModel.MIME_TYPE):\n            super().dropEvent(event)\n            return\n\n        plugin_id_bytes = mime.data(DashboardViewModel.MIME_TYPE)\n        plugin_id = bytes(plugin_id_bytes).decode()\n\n        logger.debug(\"Plugin dropped on dashboard: %s\", plugin_id)\n        self._vm.add_card(plugin_id)\n        event.acceptProposedAction()\n\n    # ---------------------------------------------------------- Context menu\n\n    def contextMenuEvent(self, event: QContextMenuEvent) -> None:\n        pos = event.globalPos()\n        widget_at_pos = self.childAt(event.pos())\n\n        menu = QMenu(self)\n        if isinstance(widget_at_pos, CrashCard):\n            plugin_id = self._plugin_id_for_widget(widget_at_pos)\n            if plugin_id:\n                remove_action = QAction(\"Remove card\", self)\n                remove_action.triggered.connect(\n                    lambda _=False, pid=plugin_id: self._vm.remove_card(pid)\n                )\n                menu.addAction(remove_action)\n        elif plugin_id := self._plugin_id_for_widget(widget_at_pos):\n            remove_action = QAction(\"Remove card\", self)\n            remove_action.triggered.connect(\n                lambda _=False, pid=plugin_id: self._vm.remove_card(pid)\n            )\n            settings_action = QAction(\"Card settings\u2026\", self)\n            settings_action.triggered.connect(\n                lambda _=False, pid=plugin_id: self._open_plugin_settings(pid)\n            )\n            menu.addActions([settings_action, remove_action])\n        else:\n            refresh_action = QAction(\"Refresh dashboard\", self)\n            refresh_action.triggered.connect(self._rebuild_cards)\n            menu.addAction(refresh_action)\n\n        menu.exec(pos)\n\n    def _plugin_id_for_widget(self, child: Optional[QWidget]) -> Optional[str]:\n        if child is None:\n            return None\n        for pid, meta in self._vm.cards().items():\n            if meta.widget is child or child.isAncestorOf(meta.widget):\n                return pid\n        return None\n\n    # --------------------------------------------------------------- Helpers\n\n    def _open_plugin_settings(self, plugin_id: str) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Call the plugin\u2019s settings UI or show fallback dialog.\"\"\"\n        plugin = self._vm._plugin_manager.get_plugin(plugin_id)  # pylint: disable=protected-access\n        if hasattr(plugin, \"open_settings\"):  # type: ignore[attr-defined]\n            plugin.open_settings(self)  # type: ignore[attr-defined]\n        else:\n            QMessageBox.information(\n                self,\n                \"Settings\",\n                f\"Plugin '{plugin_id}' does not expose a settings panel.\",\n            )\n\n    # --------------------------------------------------------------- Theming\n\n    @Slot(str)\n    def _apply_theme(self, theme_name: str) -> None:  # noqa: D401\n        \"\"\"\n        Apply QSS from the theme directory.  Blocks the UI minimally thanks to\n        async file I/O.\n        \"\"\"\n\n        async def _load_qss(name: str) -> str:  # noqa: D401\n            theme_dir = Path(QApplication.instance().property(\"themePath\"))  # type: ignore[arg-type]\n            qss_file = theme_dir / f\"{name}.qss\"\n            try:\n                return qss_file.read_text(encoding=\"utf-8\")\n            except FileNotFoundError:\n                logger.warning(\"Theme file missing: %s\", qss_file)\n                return \"\"\n\n        async def _apply() -> None:  # noqa: D401\n            qss = await _load_qss(theme_name)\n            QApplication.instance().setStyleSheet(qss)\n\n        asyncio.create_task(_apply(), name=\"dashboard.apply_theme\")\n\n    # ---------------------------------------------------------- Event filter\n\n    def event(self, e: QEvent):  # noqa: D401, N802\n        \"\"\"\n        Override event() to intercept plugin widget crashes.  Qt does not\n        natively raise Python exceptions that occur during event processing\n        inside child widgets.  By installing a global *except-hook* we can at\n        least replace the faulty widget with a CrashCard.\n        \"\"\"\n        try:\n            return super().event(e)\n        except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001\n            traceback.print_exc()\n            crashed_widget = self.childAt(self.mapFromGlobal(QCursor.pos()))\n            plugin_id = self._plugin_id_for_widget(crashed_widget)\n            if plugin_id:\n                self._handle_card_crash(plugin_id)\n            return True  # Event handled\n\n\n# -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Stand-alone test shim\n# -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\nif __name__ == \"__main__\":\n    import sys\n\n    logging.basicConfig(level=logging.DEBUG)\n\n    app = QApplication(sys.argv)\n    dash = DashboardWidget()\n    dash.resize(QSize(900, 600))\n    dash.show()\n\n    sys.exit(app.exec())\n```",

       self._lock = threading.RLock()\n\n    # ------------------------------------------------------------------ #\n    # Public API\n    # ------------------------------------------------------------------ #\n\n    def register(\n        self,\n        *,  # keyword-only for clarity\n        topic: EventTopic,\n        name: str,\n EventBus Architecture\n\n```python\n// File: /app/project/flockdesk/core/ipc/event_bus.py\n// Lines: 276-408\n\nclass EventBus:\n    \"\"\"\n    Public entry point used by every micro-front-end.\n\n    Processes talk to a shared broker, threads inside the same process share\n    exactly one :class:`EventBus` instance (thread-safe singleton).\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def subscribe(self, topic: str, handler: Handler) -> _Subscription:\n        \"\"\"\n        Register *handler* for the given *topic* pattern.\n\n        Wildcards: Use ``'*'`` to match one segment, ``'**'`` to match\n        anything recursively (see :pymod:`fnmatch`).\n        \"\"\"\n        # ... implementation\n\n    def publish(self, topic: str, payload: Any, headers: Optional[Mapping[str, Any]] = None) -> None:\n        \"\"\"\n        Fire-and-forget publish.  Safe to call from **any** thread\u2014will enqueue\n        the event into the broker's *inbound* queue.\n        \"\"\"\n        evt = Event(topic=topic, payload=payload, headers=headers or {})\n        self._inbound.put_nowait(evt)\n```\n\n### 2. Event Types Pattern\n\n```python\n// File: /app/project/flockdesk/core/ipc/event_types.py\n// Lines: 351-362\n\n@event(topic=EventTopic.SETTINGS, name=\"changed\")\n@dataclass(slots=True, frozen=True)\nclass SettingsChanged(_PayloadBase):\n    user_id: str\n    key: str\n    old_value: Any\n    new_value: Any\n    changed_at: datetime = field(\n        default_factory=lambda: datetime.now(timezone.utc)\n    )\n```\n\n### 3. SettingsService Pattern\n\n```python\n// File: /app/project/flockdesk/core/services/settings_service.py\n// Lines: 231-258\n\ndef set_value(self, namespace: str, key: str, value: Any) -> None:\n    \"\"\"\n    Update a single field in the namespace and enqueue the change for\n    persistence and event-bus broadcast.\n    \"\"\"\n    with self._lock:\n        meta = self._schemas.get(namespace)\n        instance = self._instances.get(namespace)\n        # ... validation ...\n        setattr(instance, key, value)\n        self._mark_dirty(namespace)\n```\n\n### 4. The bus supports:\n   - Topic-based routing with wildcard matching (`fnmatch`)\n   - Both sync and async handlers\n   - Process-safe communication via a broker process\n   - Request/reply pattern with correlation IDs\n\n2. **MVVM Pattern**: Each module follows MVVM:\n   - **Model**: Domain data classes (e.g., `ChatMessage`, `DashboardWidget`)\n   - **ViewModel**: Qt QObject with signals for UI binding (e.g., `ChatViewModel`, `DashboardViewModel`)\n   - **View**: Qt widgets that connect to ViewModel signals (e.g., `ChatWidget`, `DashboardWidget`)\n\n3. **Service Layer**: Core services like `SettingsService` handle cross-cutting concerns:\n   - Namespace-based settings with dataclass schemas\n   - Automatic persistence with atomic JSON writes\n   - Event-bus broadcast on changes\n\n4. **Command Pattern**: The `ShortcutCommandRegistry` encapsulates actions as first-class objects:\n   - Commands are registered with unique IDs\n   - Support for keyboard shortcuts with user customization\n   - Persistence of key bindings\n\n### Integration Points for Focus Mode\n\nThe Focus Mode feature requires integration at multiple layers:\n\n1. **Settings Layer**: Add `focus_mode_enabled` boolean to persist state\n2. **Event Layer**: Define `FOCUS_MODE_CHANGED` event type\n3. **Command Layer**: Create `ToggleFocusModeCommand` command\n4. **Menu Layer**: Add menu item in View menu\n5. **Module Layer**: Subscribe Chat and Dashboard ViewModels to the event\n\n## Implementation (For Code Modification Tasks)\n\nSince the project files are read-only, below are the complete code changes that would be implemented:\n\n### 1. Apply de-emphasis styling\n            self.setStyleSheet(\"\"\"\n                #flockdeskDashboard {\n                    opacity: 0.5;\n                }\n                #flockdeskDashboard > QWidget {\n                    background-color: rgba(128, 128, 128, 0.3);\n                }\n            \"\"\")\n            # Restore normal styling\n            self.setStyleSheet(\"\")\n            # Re-enable interaction\n            for i in range(self._grid.count()):\n                widget = self._grid.itemAt(i).widget()\n                if widget:\n                    widget.setEnabled(True)\n\n            logger.debug(\"Dashboard restored from Focus Mode\")\n\n        self.update()\n```\n\n## Summary\n\n- **Primary finding**: The Focus Mode feature requires modifications across 8 files following the application's established Event-Driven, MVVM, and Service Layer patterns.\n\n- **Key components**:\n  - `EventBus` (`/app/project/flockdesk/core/ipc/event_bus.py`) - Central pub/sub for decoupled communication\n  - `event_types.py` - Event type definitions with `@event` decorator\n  - `SettingsService` (`/app/project/flockdesk/core/services/settings_service.py`) - Persistent settings management\n  - `ShortcutCommandRegistry` (`/app/project/flockdesk/core/shortcuts/commands.py`) - Command pattern implementation\n  - `MenuBar` (`/app/project/flockdesk/core/shell/menu_bar.py`) - Application menu with View menu\n  - `ChatViewModel` / `ChatWidget` - MVVM implementation for Chat module\n  - `DashboardViewModel` / `DashboardWidget` - MVVM implementation for Dashboard module\n\n- **Architectural pattern**:\n  - **Event-Driven Architecture**: Uses `EventBus.publish()` and `EventBus.subscribe()` for loose coupling\n  - **MVVM Pattern**: ViewModels expose Qt Signals, Views bind to them via `connect()`\n  - **Service Layer**: `SettingsService` manages persistent state with namespace-based schemas\n  - **Command Pattern**: `ShortcutCommandRegistry` encapsulates actions with keyboard shortcuts\n\n- **Recommendations**:\n  1. Define the `FocusModeChanged` event payload as a frozen dataclass following existing patterns\n  2. Create a self-contained `ToggleFocusModeCommand` that accesses `SettingsService` to toggle state and `EventBus` to publish changes\n  3. In ViewModels, subscribe to `settings.focus_mode.changed` event and expose state via Qt Signal\n  4. In Views, connect to ViewModel signals to update UI (show snooze indicator, apply de-emphasis styling)\n  5. Use the existing `_SafeSlot` wrapper in MenuBar to prevent handler exceptions from crashing the UI\n\nThe implementation respects all established architectural patterns:\n- **No direct coupling**: Menu bar publishes events, modules subscribe independently\n- **Single source of truth**: `SettingsService` manages the `focus_mode_enabled` state\n- **MVVM separation**: Views react to ViewModel signals, never to events directly\n",
